### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancer

ControlPlaneLoadBalancer is optional configuration for customizing control plane behavior.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**additionalListeners**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerAdditionalListenersItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspeccontrolplaneloadbalanceradditionallistenersitems0)]|AdditionalListeners sets the additional listeners for the control plane load balancer.<br />This is only applicable to Network Load Balancer (NLB) types for the time being.||
|**additionalSecurityGroups**|[str]|AdditionalSecurityGroups sets the security groups used by the load balancer. Expected to be security group IDs<br />This is optional - if not provided new security groups will be created for the load balancer||
|**crossZoneLoadBalancing**|bool|CrossZoneLoadBalancing enables the classic ELB cross availability zone balancing.<br /><br />With cross-zone load balancing, each load balancer node for your Classic Load Balancer<br />distributes requests evenly across the registered instances in all enabled Availability Zones.<br />If cross-zone load balancing is disabled, each load balancer node distributes requests evenly across<br />the registered instances in its Availability Zone only.<br /><br />Defaults to false.||
|**disableHostsRewrite**|bool|DisableHostsRewrite disabled the hair pinning issue solution that adds the NLB's address as 127.0.0.1 to the hosts<br />file of each instance. This is by default, false.||
|**healthCheck**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerHealthCheck](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspeccontrolplaneloadbalancerhealthcheck)|health check||
|**healthCheckProtocol**|"TCP" | "SSL" | "HTTP" | "HTTPS" | "TLS" | "UDP"|HealthCheckProtocol sets the protocol type for ELB health check target<br />default value is ELBProtocolSSL||
|**ingressRules**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerIngressRulesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspeccontrolplaneloadbalanceringressrulesitems0)]|IngressRules sets the ingress rules for the control plane load balancer.||
|**loadBalancerType**|"classic" | "elb" | "alb" | "nlb" | "disabled"|LoadBalancerType sets the type for a load balancer. The default type is classic.|"classic"|
|**name**|str|Name sets the name of the classic ELB load balancer. As per AWS, the name must be unique<br />within your set of load balancers for the region, must have a maximum of 32 characters, must<br />contain only alphanumeric characters or hyphens, and cannot begin or end with a hyphen. Once<br />set, the value cannot be changed.||
|**preserveClientIP**|bool|PreserveClientIP lets the user control if preservation of client ips must be retained or not.<br />If this is enabled 6443 will be opened to 0.0.0.0/0.||
|**scheme**|"internet-facing" | "internal"|Scheme sets the scheme of the load balancer (defaults to internet-facing)|"internet-facing"|
|**subnets**|[str]|Subnets sets the subnets that should be applied to the control plane load balancer (defaults to discovered subnets for managed VPCs or an empty set for unmanaged VPCs)||

| --- | --- | --- | --- |

|**path**|str|The destination for health checks on the targets when using the protocol HTTP or HTTPS,<br />otherwise the path will be ignored.||
|**port**|str|The port the load balancer uses when performing health checks for additional target groups. When<br />not specified this value will be set for the same of listener port.||
|**protocol**|"TCP" | "HTTP" | "HTTPS"|||
|**thresholdCount**|int|The number of consecutive health check successes required before considering<br />a target healthy.||
|**timeoutSeconds**|int|The amount of time, in seconds, during which no response from a target means<br />a failed health check.||
|**unhealthyThresholdCount**|int|The number of consecutive health check failures required before considering<br />a target unhealthy.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkSubnetsItems0

SubnetSpec configures an AWS Subnet.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZone**|str|AvailabilityZone defines the availability zone to use for this subnet in the cluster's region.||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.||
|**id** `required`|str|ID defines a unique identifier to reference this resource.<br />If you're bringing your subnet, set the AWS subnet-id here, it must start with `subnet-`.<br /><br />When the VPC is managed by CAPA, and you'd like the provider to create a subnet for you,<br />the id can be set to any placeholder value that does not start with `subnet-`;<br />upon creation, the subnet AWS identifier will be populated in the `ResourceID` field and<br />the `id` field is going to be used as the subnet name. If you specify a tag<br />called `Name`, it takes precedence.||
|**ipv6CidrBlock**|str|IPv6CidrBlock is the IPv6 CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />A subnet can have an IPv4 and an IPv6 address.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isIpv6**|bool|IsIPv6 defines the subnet as an IPv6 subnet. A subnet is IPv6 when it is associated with a VPC that has IPv6 enabled.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isPublic**|bool|IsPublic defines the subnet as a public subnet. A subnet is public when it is associated with a route table that has a route to an internet gateway.||
|**natGatewayId**|str|NatGatewayID is the NAT gateway id associated with the subnet.<br />Ignored unless the subnet is managed by the provider, in which case this is set on the public subnet where the NAT gateway resides. It is then used to determine routes for private subnets in the same AZ as the public subnet.||
|**parentZoneName**|str|ParentZoneName is the zone name where the current subnet's zone is tied when<br />the zone is a Local Zone.<br /><br />The subnets in Local Zone or Wavelength Zone locations consume the ParentZoneName<br />to select the correct private route table to egress traffic to the internet.||
|**resourceID**|str|ResourceID is the subnet identifier from AWS, READ ONLY.<br />This field is populated when the provider manages the subnet.||
|**routeTableId**|str|RouteTableID is the routing table id associated with the subnet.||
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||
|**zoneType**|"availability-zone" | "local-zone" | "wavelength-zone"|ZoneType defines the type of the zone where the subnet is created.<br /><br />The valid values are availability-zone, local-zone, and wavelength-zone.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type availability-zone (regular) is always selected to create cluster<br />resources, like Load Balancers, NAT Gateways, Contol Plane nodes, etc.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type local-zone or wavelength-zone is not eligible to automatically create<br />regular cluster resources.<br /><br />The public subnet in availability-zone or local-zone is associated with regular public<br />route table with default route entry to a Internet Gateway.<br /><br />The public subnet in wavelength-zone is associated with a carrier public<br />route table with default route entry to a Carrier Gateway.<br /><br />The private subnet in the availability-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry to a NAT Gateway created in that zone.<br /><br />The private subnet in the local-zone or wavelength-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry re-using the NAT Gateway in the Region (preferred from the<br />parent zone, the zone type availability-zone in the region, or first table available).||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpc

VPC configuration.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZoneSelection**|"Ordered" | "Random"|AvailabilityZoneSelection specifies how AZs should be selected if there are more AZs<br />in a region than specified by AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit. There are 2 selection schemes:<br />Ordered - selects based on alphabetical order<br />Random - selects AZs randomly in a region<br />Defaults to Ordered|"Ordered"|
|**availabilityZoneUsageLimit**|int|AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit specifies the maximum number of availability zones (AZ) that<br />should be used in a region when automatically creating subnets. If a region has more<br />than this number of AZs then this number of AZs will be picked randomly when creating<br />default subnets. Defaults to 3|3|
|**carrierGatewayId**|str|CarrierGatewayID is the id of the internet gateway associated with the VPC,<br />for carrier network (Wavelength Zones).||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />Defaults to 10.0.0.0/16.<br />Mutually exclusive with IPAMPool.||
|**elasticIpPool**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpcElasticIPPool](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecnetworkvpcelasticippool)|elastic Ip pool||
|**emptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup**|bool|EmptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup specifies whether the default VPC security group ingress<br />and egress rules should be removed.<br /><br />By default, when creating a VPC, AWS creates a security group called `default` with ingress and egress<br />rules that allow traffic from anywhere. The group could be used as a potential surface attack and<br />it's generally suggested that the group rules are removed or modified appropriately.<br /><br />NOTE: This only applies when the VPC is managed by the Cluster API AWS controller.||
|**id**|str|ID is the vpc-id of the VPC this provider should use to create resources.||
|**internetGatewayId**|str|InternetGatewayID is the id of the internet gateway associated with the VPC.||
|**ipamPool**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpcIpamPool](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecnetworkvpcipampool)|ipam pool||
|**ipv6**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpcIPV6](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecnetworkvpcipv6)|ipv6||
|**privateDnsHostnameTypeOnLaunch**|"ip-name" | "resource-name"|PrivateDNSHostnameTypeOnLaunch is the type of hostname to assign to instances in the subnet at launch.<br />For IPv4-only and dual-stack (IPv4 and IPv6) subnets, an instance DNS name can be based on the instance IPv4 address (ip-name)<br />or the instance ID (resource-name). For IPv6 only subnets, an instance DNS name must be based on the instance ID (resource-name).||
|**secondaryCidrBlocks**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpcSecondaryCidrBlocksItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecnetworkvpcsecondarycidrblocksitems0)]|SecondaryCidrBlocks are additional CIDR blocks to be associated when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />Defaults to none. Mutually exclusive with IPAMPool. This makes sense to use if, for example, you want to use<br />a separate IP range for pods (e.g. Cilium ENI mode).||
|**subnetSchema**|"PreferPrivate" | "PreferPublic"|SubnetSchema specifies how CidrBlock should be divided on subnets in the VPC depending on the number of AZs.<br />PreferPrivate - one private subnet for each AZ plus one other subnet that will be further sub-divided for the public subnets.<br />PreferPublic - have the reverse logic of PreferPrivate, one public subnet for each AZ plus one other subnet<br />that will be further sub-divided for the private subnets.<br />Defaults to PreferPrivate|"PreferPrivate"|
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecNetworkVpcElasticIPPool

ElasticIPPool contains specific configuration to allocate Public IPv4 address (Elastic IP) from user-defined pool brought to AWS for core infrastructure resources, like NAT Gateways and Public Network Load Balancers for the API Server.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**publicIpv4Pool**|str|PublicIpv4Pool sets a custom Public IPv4 Pool used to create Elastic IP address for resources<br />created in public IPv4 subnets. Every IPv4 address, Elastic IP, will be allocated from the custom<br />Public IPv4 pool that you brought to AWS, instead of Amazon-provided pool. The public IPv4 pool<br />resource ID starts with 'ipv4pool-ec2'.||
|**publicIpv4PoolFallbackOrder**|"amazon-pool" | "none"|PublicIpv4PoolFallBackOrder defines the fallback action when the Public IPv4 Pool has been exhausted,<br />no more IPv4 address available in the pool.<br /><br />When set to 'amazon-pool', the controller check if the pool has available IPv4 address, when pool has reached the<br />IPv4 limit, the address will be claimed from Amazon-pool (default).<br /><br />When set to 'none', the controller will fail the Elastic IP allocation when the publicIpv4Pool is exhausted.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancer

SecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancer is an additional load balancer that can be used for the control plane.  An example use case is to have a separate internal load balancer for internal traffic, and a separate external load balancer for external traffic.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**additionalListeners**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancerAdditionalListenersItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecsecondarycontrolplaneloadbalanceradditionallistenersitems0)]|AdditionalListeners sets the additional listeners for the control plane load balancer.<br />This is only applicable to Network Load Balancer (NLB) types for the time being.||
|**additionalSecurityGroups**|[str]|AdditionalSecurityGroups sets the security groups used by the load balancer. Expected to be security group IDs<br />This is optional - if not provided new security groups will be created for the load balancer||
|**crossZoneLoadBalancing**|bool|CrossZoneLoadBalancing enables the classic ELB cross availability zone balancing.<br /><br />With cross-zone load balancing, each load balancer node for your Classic Load Balancer<br />distributes requests evenly across the registered instances in all enabled Availability Zones.<br />If cross-zone load balancing is disabled, each load balancer node distributes requests evenly across<br />the registered instances in its Availability Zone only.<br /><br />Defaults to false.||
|**disableHostsRewrite**|bool|DisableHostsRewrite disabled the hair pinning issue solution that adds the NLB's address as 127.0.0.1 to the hosts<br />file of each instance. This is by default, false.||
|**healthCheck**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancerHealthCheck](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecsecondarycontrolplaneloadbalancerhealthcheck)|health check||
|**healthCheckProtocol**|"TCP" | "SSL" | "HTTP" | "HTTPS" | "TLS" | "UDP"|HealthCheckProtocol sets the protocol type for ELB health check target<br />default value is ELBProtocolSSL||
|**ingressRules**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancerIngressRulesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterspecsecondarycontrolplaneloadbalanceringressrulesitems0)]|IngressRules sets the ingress rules for the control plane load balancer.||
|**loadBalancerType**|"classic" | "elb" | "alb" | "nlb" | "disabled"|LoadBalancerType sets the type for a load balancer. The default type is classic.|"classic"|
|**name**|str|Name sets the name of the classic ELB load balancer. As per AWS, the name must be unique<br />within your set of load balancers for the region, must have a maximum of 32 characters, must<br />contain only alphanumeric characters or hyphens, and cannot begin or end with a hyphen. Once<br />set, the value cannot be changed.||
|**preserveClientIP**|bool|PreserveClientIP lets the user control if preservation of client ips must be retained or not.<br />If this is enabled 6443 will be opened to 0.0.0.0/0.||
|**scheme**|"internet-facing" | "internal"|Scheme sets the scheme of the load balancer (defaults to internet-facing)|"internet-facing"|
|**subnets**|[str]|Subnets sets the subnets that should be applied to the control plane load balancer (defaults to discovered subnets for managed VPCs or an empty set for unmanaged VPCs)||

|**ebsOptimized**|bool|Indicates whether the instance is optimized for Amazon EBS I/O.||
|**enaSupport**|bool|Specifies whether enhanced networking with ENA is enabled.||
|**iamProfile**|str|The name of the IAM instance profile associated with the instance, if applicable.||
|**id** `required`|str|id||
|**imageId**|str|The ID of the AMI used to launch the instance.||
|**instanceMetadataOptions**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterStatusBastionInstanceMetadataOptions](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterstatusbastioninstancemetadataoptions)|instance metadata options||
|**instanceState**|str|The current state of the instance.||
|**marketType**|"OnDemand" | "Spot" | "CapacityBlock"|MarketType specifies the type of market for the EC2 instance. Valid values include:<br />"OnDemand" (default): The instance runs as a standard OnDemand instance.<br />"Spot": The instance runs as a Spot instance. When SpotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".<br />"CapacityBlock": The instance utilizes pre-purchased compute capacity (capacity blocks) with AWS Capacity Reservations.<br />If this value is selected, CapacityReservationID must be specified to identify the target reservation.<br />If marketType is not specified and spotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".||
|**networkInterfaceType**|str|NetworkInterfaceType is the interface type of the primary network Interface.||
|**networkInterfaces**|[str]|Specifies ENIs attached to instance||
|**nonRootVolumes**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterStatusBastionNonRootVolumesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterstatusbastionnonrootvolumesitems0)]|Configuration options for the non root storage volumes.||
|**placementGroupName**|str|PlacementGroupName specifies the name of the placement group in which to launch the instance.||
|**placementGroupPartition**|int|PlacementGroupPartition is the partition number within the placement group in which to launch the instance.<br />This value is only valid if the placement group, referred in `PlacementGroupName`, was created with<br />strategy set to partition.||
|**privateDnsName**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterStatusBastionPrivateDNSName](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterstatusbastionprivatednsname)|private Dns name||
|**privateIp**|str|The private IPv4 address assigned to the instance.||
|**publicIPOnLaunch**|bool|PublicIPOnLaunch is the option to associate a public IP on instance launch||
|**publicIp**|str|The public IPv4 address assigned to the instance, if applicable.||
|**rootVolume**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterStatusBastionRootVolume](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterstatusbastionrootvolume)|root volume||
|**securityGroupIds**|[str]|SecurityGroupIDs are one or more security group IDs this instance belongs to.||
|**spotMarketOptions**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterStatusBastionSpotMarketOptions](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclusterstatusbastionspotmarketoptions)|spot market options||
|**sshKeyName**|str|The name of the SSH key pair.||
|**subnetId**|str|The ID of the subnet of the instance.||
|**tags**|{str:str}|The tags associated with the instance.||
|**tenancy**|str|Tenancy indicates if instance should run on shared or single-tenant hardware.||
|**type**|str|||
|**userData**|str|UserData is the raw data script passed to the instance which is run upon bootstrap.<br />This field must not be base64 encoded and should only be used when running a new instance.||
|**volumeIDs**|[str]|IDs of the instance's volumes||

InstanceMetadataOptions is the metadata options for the EC2 instance.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**httpEndpoint**|"enabled" | "disabled"|Enables or disables the HTTP metadata endpoint on your instances.<br /><br />If you specify a value of disabled, you cannot access your instance metadata.<br /><br />Default: enabled|"enabled"|
|**httpPutResponseHopLimit**|int|The desired HTTP PUT response hop limit for instance metadata requests. The<br />larger the number, the further instance metadata requests can travel.<br /><br />Default: 1|1|
|**httpTokens**|"optional" | "required"|The state of token usage for your instance metadata requests.<br /><br />If the state is optional, you can choose to retrieve instance metadata with<br />or without a session token on your request. If you retrieve the IAM role<br />credentials without a token, the version 1.0 role credentials are returned.<br />If you retrieve the IAM role credentials using a valid session token, the<br />version 2.0 role credentials are returned.<br /><br />If the state is required, you must send a session token with any instance<br />metadata retrieval requests. In this state, retrieving the IAM role credentials<br />always returns the version 2.0 credentials; the version 1.0 credentials are<br />not available.<br /><br />Default: optional|"optional"|
|**instanceMetadataTags**|"enabled" | "disabled"|Set to enabled to allow access to instance tags from the instance metadata.<br />Set to disabled to turn off access to instance tags from the instance metadata.<br />For more information, see Work with instance tags using the instance metadata<br />(https://docs.aws.amazon.com/AWSEC2/latest/UserGuide/Using_Tags.html#work-with-tags-in-IMDS).<br /><br />Default: disabled|"disabled"|

|**bastion**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecBastion](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecbastion)|bastion||
|**controlPlaneEndpoint**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecControlPlaneEndpoint](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespeccontrolplaneendpoint)|control plane endpoint||
|**controlPlaneLoadBalancer**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancer](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespeccontrolplaneloadbalancer)|control plane load balancer||
|**identityRef**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecIdentityRef](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecidentityref)|identity ref||
|**imageLookupBaseOS**|str|ImageLookupBaseOS is the name of the base operating system used to look<br />up machine images when a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this<br />will be used for all cluster machines unless a machine specifies a<br />different ImageLookupBaseOS.||
|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up machine images when<br />a machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.<br />Supports substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base<br />OS and kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to look up machine images when a<br />machine does not specify an AMI. When set, this will be used for all<br />cluster machines unless a machine specifies a different ImageLookupOrg.||
|**network**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetwork](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecnetwork)|network||
|**partition**|str|Partition is the AWS security partition being used. Defaults to "aws"||
|**region**|str|The AWS Region the cluster lives in.||
|**s3Bucket**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecS3Bucket](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecs3bucket)|s3 bucket||
|**secondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancer**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancer](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecsecondarycontrolplaneloadbalancer)|secondary control plane load balancer||
|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the bastion host. Valid values are empty string (do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecBastion

Bastion contains options to configure the bastion host.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**allowedCIDRBlocks**|[str]|AllowedCIDRBlocks is a list of CIDR blocks allowed to access the bastion host.<br />They are set as ingress rules for the Bastion host's Security Group (defaults to 0.0.0.0/0).||
|**ami**|str|AMI will use the specified AMI to boot the bastion. If not specified,<br />the AMI will default to one picked out in public space.||
|**disableIngressRules**|bool|DisableIngressRules will ensure there are no Ingress rules in the bastion host's security group.<br />Requires AllowedCIDRBlocks to be empty.||
|**enabled**|bool|Enabled allows this provider to create a bastion host instance<br />with a public ip to access the VPC private network.||
|**instanceType**|str|InstanceType will use the specified instance type for the bastion. If not specified,<br />Cluster API Provider AWS will use t3.micro for all regions except us-east-1, where t2.micro<br />will be the default.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancer

ControlPlaneLoadBalancer is optional configuration for customizing control plane behavior.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**additionalListeners**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerAdditionalListenersItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespeccontrolplaneloadbalanceradditionallistenersitems0)]|AdditionalListeners sets the additional listeners for the control plane load balancer.<br />This is only applicable to Network Load Balancer (NLB) types for the time being.||
|**additionalSecurityGroups**|[str]|AdditionalSecurityGroups sets the security groups used by the load balancer. Expected to be security group IDs<br />This is optional - if not provided new security groups will be created for the load balancer||
|**crossZoneLoadBalancing**|bool|CrossZoneLoadBalancing enables the classic ELB cross availability zone balancing.<br /><br />With cross-zone load balancing, each load balancer node for your Classic Load Balancer<br />distributes requests evenly across the registered instances in all enabled Availability Zones.<br />If cross-zone load balancing is disabled, each load balancer node distributes requests evenly across<br />the registered instances in its Availability Zone only.<br /><br />Defaults to false.||
|**disableHostsRewrite**|bool|DisableHostsRewrite disabled the hair pinning issue solution that adds the NLB's address as 127.0.0.1 to the hosts<br />file of each instance. This is by default, false.||
|**healthCheck**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerHealthCheck](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespeccontrolplaneloadbalancerhealthcheck)|health check||
|**healthCheckProtocol**|"TCP" | "SSL" | "HTTP" | "HTTPS" | "TLS" | "UDP"|HealthCheckProtocol sets the protocol type for ELB health check target<br />default value is ELBProtocolSSL||
|**ingressRules**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecControlPlaneLoadBalancerIngressRulesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespeccontrolplaneloadbalanceringressrulesitems0)]|IngressRules sets the ingress rules for the control plane load balancer.||
|**loadBalancerType**|"classic" | "elb" | "alb" | "nlb" | "disabled"|LoadBalancerType sets the type for a load balancer. The default type is classic.|"classic"|
|**name**|str|Name sets the name of the classic ELB load balancer. As per AWS, the name must be unique<br />within your set of load balancers for the region, must have a maximum of 32 characters, must<br />contain only alphanumeric characters or hyphens, and cannot begin or end with a hyphen. Once<br />set, the value cannot be changed.||
|**preserveClientIP**|bool|PreserveClientIP lets the user control if preservation of client ips must be retained or not.<br />If this is enabled 6443 will be opened to 0.0.0.0/0.||
|**scheme**|"internet-facing" | "internal"|Scheme sets the scheme of the load balancer (defaults to internet-facing)|"internet-facing"|
|**subnets**|[str]|Subnets sets the subnets that should be applied to the control plane load balancer (defaults to discovered subnets for managed VPCs or an empty set for unmanaged VPCs)||

|**thresholdCount**|int|The number of consecutive health check successes required before considering<br />a target healthy.||
|**timeoutSeconds**|int|The amount of time, in seconds, during which no response from a target means<br />a failed health check.||
|**unhealthyThresholdCount**|int|The number of consecutive health check failures required before considering<br />a target unhealthy.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetworkSubnetsItems0

SubnetSpec configures an AWS Subnet.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZone**|str|AvailabilityZone defines the availability zone to use for this subnet in the cluster's region.||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.||
|**id** `required`|str|ID defines a unique identifier to reference this resource.<br />If you're bringing your subnet, set the AWS subnet-id here, it must start with `subnet-`.<br /><br />When the VPC is managed by CAPA, and you'd like the provider to create a subnet for you,<br />the id can be set to any placeholder value that does not start with `subnet-`;<br />upon creation, the subnet AWS identifier will be populated in the `ResourceID` field and<br />the `id` field is going to be used as the subnet name. If you specify a tag<br />called `Name`, it takes precedence.||
|**ipv6CidrBlock**|str|IPv6CidrBlock is the IPv6 CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />A subnet can have an IPv4 and an IPv6 address.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isIpv6**|bool|IsIPv6 defines the subnet as an IPv6 subnet. A subnet is IPv6 when it is associated with a VPC that has IPv6 enabled.<br />IPv6 is only supported in managed clusters, this field cannot be set on AWSCluster object.||
|**isPublic**|bool|IsPublic defines the subnet as a public subnet. A subnet is public when it is associated with a route table that has a route to an internet gateway.||
|**natGatewayId**|str|NatGatewayID is the NAT gateway id associated with the subnet.<br />Ignored unless the subnet is managed by the provider, in which case this is set on the public subnet where the NAT gateway resides. It is then used to determine routes for private subnets in the same AZ as the public subnet.||
|**parentZoneName**|str|ParentZoneName is the zone name where the current subnet's zone is tied when<br />the zone is a Local Zone.<br /><br />The subnets in Local Zone or Wavelength Zone locations consume the ParentZoneName<br />to select the correct private route table to egress traffic to the internet.||
|**resourceID**|str|ResourceID is the subnet identifier from AWS, READ ONLY.<br />This field is populated when the provider manages the subnet.||
|**routeTableId**|str|RouteTableID is the routing table id associated with the subnet.||
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||
|**zoneType**|"availability-zone" | "local-zone" | "wavelength-zone"|ZoneType defines the type of the zone where the subnet is created.<br /><br />The valid values are availability-zone, local-zone, and wavelength-zone.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type availability-zone (regular) is always selected to create cluster<br />resources, like Load Balancers, NAT Gateways, Contol Plane nodes, etc.<br /><br />Subnet with zone type local-zone or wavelength-zone is not eligible to automatically create<br />regular cluster resources.<br /><br />The public subnet in availability-zone or local-zone is associated with regular public<br />route table with default route entry to a Internet Gateway.<br /><br />The public subnet in wavelength-zone is associated with a carrier public<br />route table with default route entry to a Carrier Gateway.<br /><br />The private subnet in the availability-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry to a NAT Gateway created in that zone.<br /><br />The private subnet in the local-zone or wavelength-zone is associated with a private route table with<br />the default route entry re-using the NAT Gateway in the Region (preferred from the<br />parent zone, the zone type availability-zone in the region, or first table available).||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetworkVpc

VPC configuration.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**availabilityZoneSelection**|"Ordered" | "Random"|AvailabilityZoneSelection specifies how AZs should be selected if there are more AZs<br />in a region than specified by AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit. There are 2 selection schemes:<br />Ordered - selects based on alphabetical order<br />Random - selects AZs randomly in a region<br />Defaults to Ordered|"Ordered"|
|**availabilityZoneUsageLimit**|int|AvailabilityZoneUsageLimit specifies the maximum number of availability zones (AZ) that<br />should be used in a region when automatically creating subnets. If a region has more<br />than this number of AZs then this number of AZs will be picked randomly when creating<br />default subnets. Defaults to 3|3|
|**carrierGatewayId**|str|CarrierGatewayID is the id of the internet gateway associated with the VPC,<br />for carrier network (Wavelength Zones).||
|**cidrBlock**|str|CidrBlock is the CIDR block to be used when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />Defaults to 10.0.0.0/16.<br />Mutually exclusive with IPAMPool.||
|**elasticIpPool**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetworkVpcElasticIPPool](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecnetworkvpcelasticippool)|elastic Ip pool||
|**emptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup**|bool|EmptyRoutesDefaultVPCSecurityGroup specifies whether the default VPC security group ingress<br />and egress rules should be removed.<br /><br />By default, when creating a VPC, AWS creates a security group called `default` with ingress and egress<br />rules that allow traffic from anywhere. The group could be used as a potential surface attack and<br />it's generally suggested that the group rules are removed or modified appropriately.<br /><br />NOTE: This only applies when the VPC is managed by the Cluster API AWS controller.||
|**id**|str|ID is the vpc-id of the VPC this provider should use to create resources.||
|**internetGatewayId**|str|InternetGatewayID is the id of the internet gateway associated with the VPC.||
|**ipamPool**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetworkVpcIpamPool](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecnetworkvpcipampool)|ipam pool||
|**ipv6**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetworkVpcIPV6](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecnetworkvpcipv6)|ipv6||
|**privateDnsHostnameTypeOnLaunch**|"ip-name" | "resource-name"|PrivateDNSHostnameTypeOnLaunch is the type of hostname to assign to instances in the subnet at launch.<br />For IPv4-only and dual-stack (IPv4 and IPv6) subnets, an instance DNS name can be based on the instance IPv4 address (ip-name)<br />or the instance ID (resource-name). For IPv6 only subnets, an instance DNS name must be based on the instance ID (resource-name).||
|**secondaryCidrBlocks**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetworkVpcSecondaryCidrBlocksItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecnetworkvpcsecondarycidrblocksitems0)]|SecondaryCidrBlocks are additional CIDR blocks to be associated when the provider creates a managed VPC.<br />Defaults to none. Mutually exclusive with IPAMPool. This makes sense to use if, for example, you want to use<br />a separate IP range for pods (e.g. Cilium ENI mode).||
|**subnetSchema**|"PreferPrivate" | "PreferPublic"|SubnetSchema specifies how CidrBlock should be divided on subnets in the VPC depending on the number of AZs.<br />PreferPrivate - one private subnet for each AZ plus one other subnet that will be further sub-divided for the public subnets.<br />PreferPublic - have the reverse logic of PreferPrivate, one public subnet for each AZ plus one other subnet<br />that will be further sub-divided for the private subnets.<br />Defaults to PreferPrivate|"PreferPrivate"|
|**tags**|{str:str}|Tags is a collection of tags describing the resource.||
### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecNetworkVpcElasticIPPool

ElasticIPPool contains specific configuration to allocate Public IPv4 address (Elastic IP) from user-defined pool brought to AWS for core infrastructure resources, like NAT Gateways and Public Network Load Balancers for the API Server.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**publicIpv4Pool**|str|PublicIpv4Pool sets a custom Public IPv4 Pool used to create Elastic IP address for resources<br />created in public IPv4 subnets. Every IPv4 address, Elastic IP, will be allocated from the custom<br />Public IPv4 pool that you brought to AWS, instead of Amazon-provided pool. The public IPv4 pool<br />resource ID starts with 'ipv4pool-ec2'.||
|**publicIpv4PoolFallbackOrder**|"amazon-pool" | "none"|PublicIpv4PoolFallBackOrder defines the fallback action when the Public IPv4 Pool has been exhausted,<br />no more IPv4 address available in the pool.<br /><br />When set to 'amazon-pool', the controller check if the pool has available IPv4 address, when pool has reached the<br />IPv4 limit, the address will be claimed from Amazon-pool (default).<br /><br />When set to 'none', the controller will fail the Elastic IP allocation when the publicIpv4Pool is exhausted.||

### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancer

SecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancer is an additional load balancer that can be used for the control plane.  An example use case is to have a separate internal load balancer for internal traffic, and a separate external load balancer for external traffic.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**additionalListeners**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancerAdditionalListenersItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecsecondarycontrolplaneloadbalanceradditionallistenersitems0)]|AdditionalListeners sets the additional listeners for the control plane load balancer.<br />This is only applicable to Network Load Balancer (NLB) types for the time being.||
|**additionalSecurityGroups**|[str]|AdditionalSecurityGroups sets the security groups used by the load balancer. Expected to be security group IDs<br />This is optional - if not provided new security groups will be created for the load balancer||
|**crossZoneLoadBalancing**|bool|CrossZoneLoadBalancing enables the classic ELB cross availability zone balancing.<br /><br />With cross-zone load balancing, each load balancer node for your Classic Load Balancer<br />distributes requests evenly across the registered instances in all enabled Availability Zones.<br />If cross-zone load balancing is disabled, each load balancer node distributes requests evenly across<br />the registered instances in its Availability Zone only.<br /><br />Defaults to false.||
|**disableHostsRewrite**|bool|DisableHostsRewrite disabled the hair pinning issue solution that adds the NLB's address as 127.0.0.1 to the hosts<br />file of each instance. This is by default, false.||
|**healthCheck**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancerHealthCheck](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecsecondarycontrolplaneloadbalancerhealthcheck)|health check||
|**healthCheckProtocol**|"TCP" | "SSL" | "HTTP" | "HTTPS" | "TLS" | "UDP"|HealthCheckProtocol sets the protocol type for ELB health check target<br />default value is ELBProtocolSSL||
|**ingressRules**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSClusterTemplateSpecTemplateSpecSecondaryControlPlaneLoadBalancerIngressRulesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsclustertemplatespectemplatespecsecondarycontrolplaneloadbalanceringressrulesitems0)]|IngressRules sets the ingress rules for the control plane load balancer.||
|**loadBalancerType**|"classic" | "elb" | "alb" | "nlb" | "disabled"|LoadBalancerType sets the type for a load balancer. The default type is classic.|"classic"|
|**name**|str|Name sets the name of the classic ELB load balancer. As per AWS, the name must be unique<br />within your set of load balancers for the region, must have a maximum of 32 characters, must<br />contain only alphanumeric characters or hyphens, and cannot begin or end with a hyphen. Once<br />set, the value cannot be changed.||
|**preserveClientIP**|bool|PreserveClientIP lets the user control if preservation of client ips must be retained or not.<br />If this is enabled 6443 will be opened to 0.0.0.0/0.||
|**scheme**|"internet-facing" | "internal"|Scheme sets the scheme of the load balancer (defaults to internet-facing)|"internet-facing"|
|**subnets**|[str]|Subnets sets the subnets that should be applied to the control plane load balancer (defaults to discovered subnets for managed VPCs or an empty set for unmanaged VPCs)||

|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up the image for this<br />machine It will be ignored if an explicit AMI is set. Supports<br />substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base OS and<br />kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||

|**instanceType**|str|InstanceType is the type of instance to create. Example: m4.xlarge||
|**marketType**|"OnDemand" | "Spot" | "CapacityBlock"|MarketType specifies the type of market for the EC2 instance. Valid values include:<br />"OnDemand" (default): The instance runs as a standard OnDemand instance.<br />"Spot": The instance runs as a Spot instance. When SpotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".<br />"CapacityBlock": The instance utilizes pre-purchased compute capacity (capacity blocks) with AWS Capacity Reservations.<br />If this value is selected, CapacityReservationID must be specified to identify the target reservation.<br />If marketType is not specified and spotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".||
|**name**|str|The name of the launch template.||
|**nonRootVolumes**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplateNonRootVolumesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsmachinepoolspecawslaunchtemplatenonrootvolumesitems0)]|Configuration options for the non root storage volumes.||

Value range is 100 to 200.<br />If you specify MaxHealthyPercentage , you must also specify MinHealthyPercentage , and the difference between<br />them cannot be greater than 100.<br />A larger range increases the number of instances that can be replaced at the same time.||
|**minHealthyPercentage**|int|The amount of capacity as a percentage in ASG that must remain healthy<br />during an instance refresh. The default is 90.||
|**strategy**|str|The strategy to use for the instance refresh. The only valid value is Rolling.<br />A rolling update is an update that is applied to all instances in an Auto<br />Scaling group until all instances have been updated.||

|**conditions**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSMachinePoolStatusConditionsItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsmachinepoolstatusconditionsitems0)]|Conditions defines current service state of the AWSMachinePool.||
|**failureMessage**|str|FailureMessage will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the Machine and will contain a more verbose string suitable<br />for logging and human consumption.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the Machine's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of Machines<br />can be added as events to the Machine object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**failureReason**|str|FailureReason will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the Machine and will contain a succinct value suitable<br />for machine interpretation.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the Machine's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. Examples<br />of terminal errors would be invalid combinations of settings in the<br />spec, values that are unsupported by the controller, or the<br />responsible controller itself being critically misconfigured.<br /><br />Any transient errors that occur during the reconciliation of Machines<br />can be added as events to the Machine object and/or logged in the<br />controller's output.||
|**infrastructureMachineKind**|str|InfrastructureMachineKind is the kind of the infrastructure resources behind MachinePool Machines.||
|**instances**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSMachinePoolStatusInstancesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsmachinepoolstatusinstancesitems0)]|Instances contains the status for each instance in the pool||
|**launchTemplateID**|str|The ID of the launch template||
|**launchTemplateVersion**|str|The version of the launch template||
|**ready**|bool|Ready is true when the provider resource is ready.||
|**replicas**|int|Replicas is the most recently observed number of replicas||

The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. When SpotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".<br />"CapacityBlock": The instance utilizes pre-purchased compute capacity (capacity blocks) with AWS Capacity Reservations.<br />If this value is selected, CapacityReservationID must be specified to identify the target reservation.<br />If marketType is not specified and spotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".||

|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up the image for this<br />machine It will be ignored if an explicit AMI is set. Supports<br />substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base OS and<br />kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to use for image lookup if AMI is not set.||
|**instanceID**|str|InstanceID is the EC2 instance ID for this machine.||

|**instanceType** `required`|str|InstanceType is the type of instance to create. Example: m4.xlarge||
|**marketType**|"OnDemand" | "Spot" | "CapacityBlock"|MarketType specifies the type of market for the EC2 instance. Valid values include:<br />"OnDemand" (default): The instance runs as a standard OnDemand instance.<br />"Spot": The instance runs as a Spot instance. When SpotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".<br />"CapacityBlock": The instance utilizes pre-purchased compute capacity (capacity blocks) with AWS Capacity Reservations.<br />If this value is selected, CapacityReservationID must be specified to identify the target reservation.<br />If marketType is not specified and spotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".||

|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the instance. Valid values are empty string (do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||

#### Attributes

|**noProxy**|[str]|NoProxy is the list of domains to not proxy for Ignition.<br />Specifies a list of strings to hosts that should be excluded from proxying.<br /><br />Each value is represented by:<br />- An IP address prefix (1.2.3.4)<br />- An IP address prefix in CIDR notation (1.2.3.4/8)<br />- A domain name<br />- A domain name matches that name and all subdomains<br />- A domain name with a leading . matches subdomains only<br />- A special DNS label (*), indicates that no proxying should be done<br /><br />An IP address prefix and domain name can also include a literal port number (1.2.3.4:80).||

AWSLaunchTemplate specifies the launch template to use to create the managed node group. If AWSLaunchTemplate is specified, certain node group configuraions outside of launch template are prohibited (https://docs.aws.amazon.com/eks/latest/userguide/launch-templates.html).

#### Attributes

|**iamInstanceProfile**|str|The name or the Amazon Resource Name (ARN) of the instance profile associated<br />with the IAM role for the instance. The instance profile contains the IAM<br />role.||
|**imageLookupBaseOS**|str|ImageLookupBaseOS is the name of the base operating system to use for<br />image lookup the AMI is not set.||
|**imageLookupFormat**|str|ImageLookupFormat is the AMI naming format to look up the image for this<br />machine It will be ignored if an explicit AMI is set. Supports<br />substitutions for {{.BaseOS}} and {{.K8sVersion}} with the base OS and<br />kubernetes version, respectively. The BaseOS will be the value in<br />ImageLookupBaseOS or ubuntu (the default), and the kubernetes version as<br />defined by the packages produced by kubernetes/release without v as a<br />prefix: 1.13.0, 1.12.5-mybuild.1, or 1.17.3. For example, the default<br />image format of capa-ami-{{.BaseOS}}-?{{.K8sVersion}}-* will end up<br />searching for AMIs that match the pattern capa-ami-ubuntu-?1.18.0-* for a<br />Machine that is targeting kubernetes v1.18.0 and the ubuntu base OS. See<br />also: https://golang.org/pkg/text/template/||
|**imageLookupOrg**|str|ImageLookupOrg is the AWS Organization ID to use for image lookup if AMI is not set.||
|**instanceMetadataOptions**|[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSManagedMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplateInstanceMetadataOptions](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsmanagedmachinepoolspecawslaunchtemplateinstancemetadataoptions)|instance metadata options||
|**instanceType**|str|InstanceType is the type of instance to create. Example: m4.xlarge||
|**marketType**|"OnDemand" | "Spot" | "CapacityBlock"|MarketType specifies the type of market for the EC2 instance. Valid values include:<br />"OnDemand" (default): The instance runs as a standard OnDemand instance.<br />"Spot": The instance runs as a Spot instance. When SpotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".<br />"CapacityBlock": The instance utilizes pre-purchased compute capacity (capacity blocks) with AWS Capacity Reservations.<br />If this value is selected, CapacityReservationID must be specified to identify the target reservation.<br />If marketType is not specified and spotMarketOptions is provided, the marketType defaults to "Spot".||
|**name**|str|The name of the launch template.||
|**nonRootVolumes**|[[InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2AWSManagedMachinePoolSpecAwsLaunchTemplateNonRootVolumesItems0](#infrastructureclusterxk8siov1beta2awsmanagedmachinepoolspecawslaunchtemplatenonrootvolumesitems0)]|Configuration options for the non root storage volumes.||

|**sshKeyName**|str|SSHKeyName is the name of the ssh key to attach to the instance. Valid values are empty string<br />(do not use SSH keys), a valid SSH key name, or omitted (use the default SSH key name)||
|**versionNumber**|int|VersionNumber is the version of the launch template that is applied.<br />Typically a new version is created when at least one of the following happens:<br />1) A new launch template spec is applied.<br />2) One or more parameters in an existing template is changed.<br />3) A new AMI is discovered.||

|**failureMessage**|str|FailureMessage will be set in the event that there is a terminal problem<br />reconciling the MachinePool and will contain a more verbose string suitable<br />for logging and human consumption.<br /><br />This field should not be set for transitive errors that a controller<br />faces that are expected to be fixed automatically over<br />time (like service outages), but instead indicate that something is<br />fundamentally wrong with the MachinePool's spec or the configuration of<br />the controller, and that manual intervention is required. ### InfrastructureClusterxK8sIoV1beta2ROSAMachinePoolSpecUpdateConfigRollingUpdate

RollingUpdate specifies MaxUnavailable & MaxSurge number of nodes during update.

#### Attributes

| name | type | description | default value |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
|**maxSurge**|int | str|MaxSurge is the maximum number of nodes that can be provisioned above the desired number of nodes.<br />Value can be an absolute number (ex: 5) or a percentage of desired nodes (ex: 10%).<br />Absolute number is calculated from percentage by rounding up.<br /><br />MaxSurge can not be 0 if MaxUnavailable is 0, default is 1.<br />Both MaxSurge & MaxUnavailable must use the same units (absolute value or percentage).<br /><br />Example: when MaxSurge is set to 30%, new nodes can be provisioned immediately<br />when the rolling update starts, such that the total number of old and new<br />nodes do not exceed 130% of desired nodes. Once old nodes have been<br />deleted, new nodes can be provisioned, ensuring that total number of nodes<br />running at any time during the update is at most 130% of desired nodes.|1|
|**maxUnavailable**|int | str|MaxUnavailable is the maximum number of nodes that can be unavailable during the update.<br />Value can be an absolute number (ex: 5) or a percentage of desired nodes (ex: 10%).<br />Absolute number is calculated from percentage by rounding down.<br /><br />MaxUnavailable can not be 0 if MaxSurge is 0, default is 0.<br />Both MaxUnavailable & MaxSurge must use the same units (absolute value or percentage).<br /><br />Example: when MaxUnavailable is set to 30%, old nodes can be deleted down to 70% of<br />desired nodes immediately when the rolling update starts. Once new nodes<br />are ready, more old nodes be deleted, followed by provisioning new nodes,<br />ensuring that the total number of nodes available at all times during the<br />update is at least 70% of desired nodes.|0|
